وأما قول الشافعي فيه فأخبرنا الشيخ أبو الأعز قراتكين بن الأسعد الازجي قال أخبرنا أبو محمد الحسن بن علي بن محمد الجوهري قال أنا أبو الحسن علي بن عبد العزيز بن مردك قال أنا أبو محمد عبد الرحمن بن أبي حاتم الرازي قال ثنا يونس بن عبد الأعلى المصري قال سمعت الشافعي يقول لأن يبتلى المرء بكل ما نهى الله عنه سوى الشرك خير له من الكلام ولقد أطلعت من أهل الكلام على شيء ما ظننت أن مسلما يقول ذلك. وأخبرنا قراتكين بن الأسعد قال أنا الحسن ابن علي قال أنا علي بن عبد العزيز قال أخبرنا عبد الرحمن بن أبي حاتم قال ثنا أحمد بن أصرم المزني من ولد عبد الله بن المغفل قال قال أبو ثور سمعت الشافعي يقول ما تردى أحد في الكلام فأفلح. وأخبرنا الشيخ الفقيه أبو الفتح نصر الله ابن محمد بن عبد القوي المصيصي بدمشق قال أنا أبو البركات أحمد بن عبد الله بن علي بن طاوس المقري البغدادي بدمشق قال أخبرنا أبو القسم عبيد الله بن أحمد بن عثمان الصيرفي قال لنا أبو علي الحسن بن الحسين بن حمكان الفقيه قال حدثني الزبير بن عبد الواحد قال حدثني أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف الهروي بدمشق قال رأيت في كتاب عن أبي بكر محمد بن الجنيد صاحب أبي ثور قال سمعت أبا ثور يقول سمعت الشافعي يقول من ابتلي بالكلام لم يفلح. وأخبرنا الفقيه أبو الفتح قال أنا البركات البغدادي قال أنا أبو القسم الأزهري قال أنا أبو علي بن حمكان قال حدثني الزبير بن عبد الواحد قال حدثني محمد بن يحيى ابن آدم الحرشي بمصر قال ثنا محمد بن عبد الله بن عبد الحكم قال سمعت الشافعي يقول لو علم الناس ما في الكلام في الأهواء لفروا منه كما يفر من الأسد. وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو الأعز الأزجي قال أنا أبو محمد الجوهري قال أنا أبو الحسن بن مردك قال أنا أبو محمد بن أبي حاتم الرازي قال ثنا الربيع بن سليمان المرادي قال رأيت الشافعي وهو نازل في الدرجة وقوم في المجالس يتكلمون بشيء من الكلام فصاح فقال إما أن تجاورونا بخير وإما أن تقوموا عنا فإنما عنى الشافعي بذلك كلام البدعي المخالف عند اعتباره للدليل الشرعي فقد بين زكريا بن يحيى الساجي في روايته هذه الحكاية عن الربيع أنه أراد بالنهي عن الكلام قوما تكلموا في القدر فلذلك حكم بالتبديع ويدل عليه ما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد ابن الفضل الفراوي قال أنا أبو عثمان إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن الصابوني قال أنا خالي أبو الفضل عمر بن إبراهيم الزاهد قال أنا أبو العباس عبد محمد بن جعفر البوشنجي قال ثنا محمد بن إسحق بن خزيمة قال سمعت يونس بن عبد الأعلى يقول جئت الشافعي بعدما كلم حفص الفرد فقال غبت عنايا أبا موسى لقد أطلعت من أهل الكلام على شيء وا والله ما توهمته قط ولأن يبتلى المرء بكل ما نهي عنه ما خلا الشرك بالله خير له من أن يبتلى بالكلام فالشافعي رحمه الله إنما عنى بمقاله كلام حفص الفرد القدري وأمثاله ويدل عليه ما أخبرنا قراتكين بن الأسعد قال ثنا الحسن ابن علي قال أنا علي بن عبد العزيز قال أنا عبد الرحمن بن أبي حاتم قال ثنا يونس بن عبد الأعلى قال قال لي الشافعي يعلم الله يا أبا موسى لقد أطلعت من أصحاب الكلام على شيء لم أظنه يكون ولأن يبتلى المرء بكل ذنب نهى الله عز وجل عنه ما عدا الشرك به خير له من الكلام قال يونس يعني في الأهواء
As for the statement of al-Shafi'i concerning it: the shaykh Abu al-A'izz Qiratakin ibn al-As'ad al-Azaji informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jawhari informed us, saying: Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Mardak informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim al-Razi informed us, saying: Yunus ibn 'Abd al-A'la al-Misri narrated to us, saying: I heard al-Shafi'i say: 'That a person be afflicted with everything that Allah has forbidden except shirk is better for him than kalam. Indeed, I have seen from the people of kalam something that I never thought any Muslim would say.' And Qiratakin ibn al-As'ad informed us, saying: al-Hasan ibn 'Ali informed us, saying: 'Ali ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz informed us, saying: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim informed us, saying: Ahmad ibn Asram al-Muzani from the descendants of 'Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal narrated to us, saying: Abu Thawr said: I heard al-Shafi'i say: 'No one engaged in kalam and succeeded.' And the faqih shaykh Abu al-Fath Nasrallah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Qawi al-Masisi informed us in Damascus, saying: Abu al-Barakat Ahmad ibn 'Abdullah ibn 'Ali ibn Tawus al-Muqri al-Baghdadi informed us in Damascus, saying: Abu al-Qasim 'Ubaydullah ibn Ahmad ibn 'Uthman al-Sayrafi informed us, saying: Abu 'Ali al-Hasan ibn al-Husayn ibn Hamkan al-Faqih narrated to us, saying: al-Zubayr ibn 'Abd al-Wahid narrated to me, saying: Abu 'Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Hirawi narrated to me in Damascus, saying: I saw in a book from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Junayd, companion of Abu Thawr, saying: I heard Abu Thawr say: I heard al-Shafi'i say: 'Whoever is afflicted by kalam will not succeed.' And the faqih Abu al-Fath informed us, saying: al-Barakat al-Baghdadi informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari informed us, saying: Abu 'Ali ibn Hamkan informed us, saying: al-Zubayr ibn 'Abd al-Wahid narrated to me, saying: Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Adam al-Hirshi narrated to me in Egypt, saying: Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn 'Abd al-Hakam narrated to us, saying: I heard al-Shafi'i say: 'If people knew what is in kalam concerning desires (ahwa'), they would flee from it as they flee from a lion.' And the shaykh Abu al-A'izz al-Azaji informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad al-Jawhari informed us, saying: Abu al-Hasan ibn Mardak informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Hatim al-Razi informed us, saying: al-Rabi' ibn Sulayman al-Muradi narrated to us, saying: I saw al-Shafi'i while he was descending the steps and people in the gatherings were speaking about something of kalam, so he shouted and said: 'Either you neighbor us with good, or leave us.' For al-Shafi'i meant by that the kalam of the innovator (al-bid'i) who opposes, when considering the legal evidence. Zakariyya ibn Yahya al-Saji explained in this report from al-Rabi' that he meant by forbidding kalam a people who spoke about predestination (al-qadar), and therefore he ruled them as innovators. And it is indicated by what the shaykh Abu 'Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi informed us, saying: Abu 'Uthman Isma'il ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni informed us, saying: my maternal uncle Abu al-Fadl 'Umar ibn Ibrahim al-Zahid informed us, saying: Abu al-'Abbas 'Abd Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Bushanji informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzayma narrated to us, saying: I heard Yunus ibn 'Abd al-A'la say: I came to al-Shafi'i after he spoke to Hafs al-Fard, and he said: 'I was inattentive to me, O Abu Musa? I have indeed seen from the people of kalam something that, by Allah, I never imagined. And that a person be afflicted with everything that has been forbidden except shirk with Allah is better for him than to be afflicted with kalam.' So al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, meant by his statement the kalam of Hafs al-Fard al-Qadari and his likes. And it is indicated by what Qiratakin ibn al-As'ad informed us, saying: al-Hasan ibn 'Ali narrated to us, saying: 'Ali ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz informed us, saying: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim informed us, saying: Yunus ibn 'Abd al-A'la narrated to us, saying: al-Shafi'i said to me: 'Allah knows, O Abu Musa, I have seen from the companions of kalam something I did not think could be. And that a person be afflicted with every sin that Allah Almighty has forbidden except shirk with Him is better for him than kalam.' Yunus said: meaning concerning desires (ahwa').
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objection, raised by readers who encounter al-Shafi'i's severe condemnations of kalam, is that al-Shafi'i apparently condemned all kalam absolutely. The author, Ibn Asakir, answers by demonstrating through multiple chains of transmission and contextual evidence that al-Shafi'i's censure was specifically directed at the kalam of the innovators (ahl al-ahwa'), particularly the Qadariyya who debated predestination. The passage begins by citing several reports: Yunus ibn 'Abd al-A'la heard al-Shafi'i say that being afflicted with all sins except shirk is better than kalam, and that he saw from the people of kalam something he never thought any Muslim would say. Another report from Abu Thawr quotes al-Shafi'i saying no one engaged in kalam and succeeded. A third report says whoever is afflicted by kalam will not succeed. A fourth says if people knew what kalam contains of desires, they would flee it like lions. Then comes the key report from al-Rabi' ibn Sulayman: he saw al-Shafi'i shout at people speaking about kalam and order them to leave. The author immediately interprets: al-Shafi'i meant by that the kalam of the innovator who opposes legal evidence. Zakariyya al-Saji's interpretation of this incident clarifies that al-Shafi'i was forbidding the kalam of those who spoke about qadar (predestination). This is corroborated by the story of Hafs al-Fard, a famous Qadari theologian. Al-Shafi'i, after debating Hafs, expressed shock and said being afflicted with all sins except shirk is better than being afflicted with kalam. The author explicitly states that al-Shafi'i meant the kalam of Hafs al-Fard and his likes. The final report from Yunus states that al-Shafi'i's criticism was about kalam in the context of desires (ahwa'). Thus the apparent blanket condemnation is restricted to the kalam of the innovators, specifically those who engage in theological speculation based on desires rather than the revealed sources. This is a defense of the discipline of kalam when practiced within the bounds of orthodoxy.

Key Terms
الكلام
الأهواء
القدر
البدعي
المخالف
حفص الفرد
الشافعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Shafi'i completely forbade all theological discussion (kalam) as a whole.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i's harsh statements were specifically directed at the kalam of the innovators, particularly the Qadariyya who debated predestination based on desires, not at the disciplined science of kalam practiced within the bounds of revelation.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what type of kalam did al-Shafi'i condemn in his statements?
A) All forms of kalam without exception
B) Only the kalam of the Qadariyya and similar innovators
C) Only the kalam of the Ash'aris
D) Only kalam that contradicts fiqh

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's condemnations of kalam were not absolute; they targeted the innovative theological speculations of the Qadariyya and others who argued based on desires, thus preserving the legitimacy of orthodox kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a scholar's strong condemnation of a practice, do you rush to adopt that judgment as absolute, or do you pause to investigate the context—even if it means admitting you were too quick to judge? What is your heart's default response?
?
This lesson shows that even al-Shafi'i's sharpest words were directed at specific people and situations, not at all who engage in theological discussion. Have you ever dismissed an entire field of study (or group of Muslims) based on a single quote you heard out of context? Will you go back and re-examine that judgment today, even if it means humbling yourself?
?
Al-Shafi'i condemned those who argued from desires rather than evidence. Where in your own life—whether in religious discussions or personal opinions—are you speaking from your desires rather than from clear guidance? What would it cost you to lay aside your preferences and submit to the evidence?

4 min
Shafi'i's Strategy in Debating Innovators
Shafi'i states his approach to debating innovators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Shafi'i's unique stance in debating innovators and why he wishes for their error to become public.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i debated to expose error in innovators, not to win.

This passage presents a rare, personal statement from Imam al-Shafi'i about his debating strategy. Through an authentic chain of narration, we learn that he approached discussions with innovators differently: he actually hoped they would err so that their falsehood would be made clear to the community. This reveals a protective, truth-centered methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the isnad and statement
Read the full Arabic text including the chain of narrators. Then read the translation. Note that the isnad attests to the reliability of the report.
The names may have minor spelling variations; focus on the meaning.
2
Understand the contrast
Al-Shafi'i says he never wished for anyone to err except an innovator. Identify what this implies about his debates with non-innovators: he did not wish them to err.
This highlights his intention in debates: for innovators, exposure of error is a goal.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Why would he want the innovator's error to be exposed? Consider the benefit to the community: preventing the spread of false beliefs.
This is a strategic, not personal, desire—it aims to protect the faith.

وأخبرنا الشيخ الفقيه أبو الفتح نصر الله بن محمد الشافعي قال أنا أبو البركات أحمد بن عبد الله المقرى قال أنا أبو القسم عبيد الله أحمد بن الصير فى قال : أنا أبو على بن حمكان قال حدثنى الزبير بن عبد الواحد قال حدثني عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الشافعي ، قال ثنا محمد بن بن إسحق الخفاف قال سمعت أبا العباس البغدادى يقول : سمعت الحسن بن عبد العزيز الجروى يقول سمعت الشافعي يقول : ما ناظرت أحدا أحببت أن يخطئ إلا صاحب بدعة فإني أحب أن ينكشف أمره للناس.
And the shaykh, the faqih Abu al-Fath Nasrallah ibn Muhammad al-Shafi'i informed us, he said: Abu al-Barakat Ahmad ibn Abdullah al-Muqri' informed us, he said: Abu al-Qasim Ubaydullah Ahmad ibn al-Sayyar informed us, he said: Abu Ali ibn Hamkan informed us, he said: al-Zubayr ibn Abd al-Wahid narrated to me, he said: Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shafi'i narrated to me, he said: Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Khaffaf narrated to us, he said: I heard Abu al-Abbas al-Baghdadi say: I heard al-Hasan ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Jarawi say: I heard al-Shafi'i say: I have never debated anyone whom I wished would err except an innovator, for I love that his matter be exposed to the people.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a report of a statement by Imam al-Shafi'i regarding his attitude in debates with innovators. The chain of transmission includes several narrators, ultimately reaching al-Shafi'i himself. The core statement is: 'I have never debated anyone whom I wished would err except an innovator, for I love that his matter be exposed to the people.' This indicates that al-Shafi'i's intention in debating innovators is not to win a polite exchange, but to reveal their error publicly so that people become aware of their deviation. The phrase 'I wished would err' is striking: it shows that for the innovator, al-Shafi'i actually hopes for their mistake to become evident, because that serves the greater good of protecting the community from their false ideas. In contrast, in debates with others, he would not wish for them to err. This reflects a strategic approach to safeguarding orthodox creed.

Key Terms
صاحب بدعة
ينكشف أمره
الشافعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Shafi'i was hostile to all debate and wished for everyone to err.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i explicitly says he never wished anyone to err except an innovator, indicating his debates with others were conducted without such a wish.

Checkpoint
What does al-Shafi'i say about his wish when debating an innovator?
A) He wishes that the innovator would be guided.
B) He wishes that the innovator would err so his matter is exposed.
C) He wishes that the debate would end quickly.
D) He wishes that the innovator would apologize.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i uniquely desired that innovators err in debate so their falsehoods would be made public to protect the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you enter a debate about religious matters, do you genuinely hope the truth is revealed, even if it means you were wrong? Al-Shafi'i loved that the innovator's error be exposed. How would you react if your own error were exposed? Commit to seeking truth above your own ego.
?
Think of a time you disagreed with someone over a religious practice you believe is an innovation. Did you wish for their error to be made clear, or were you more focused on winning the argument? What did your heart intend? This lesson forces you to examine your motive: was it love for truth or something else?
?
Al-Shafi'i's desire for the innovator to err was rooted in care for the community, not personal animosity. Is there anyone you dislike because of their beliefs? Ask yourself: can you genuinely wish for the truth to be known for their sake, even if it means you are proven wrong? Pledge to purify your heart tonight.

The Mihna and al-Muzani's Reluctant Testimony
Al-Bayhaqi narrates al-Muzani's story to show the context of kalam during the mihna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mihna forced scholars like al-Muzani to publicly affirm the Quran as uncreated, despite their initial reluctance to engage in kalam.

Core Idea
Even cautious scholars declared the Quran uncreated when directly challenged.

This lesson presents a vivid historical narration from the mihna (inquisition) over the createdness of the Quran. Through al-Muzani, a leading student of Imam al-Shafi'i, we see how righteous scholars balanced piety, fear of rulers, and the need to defend truth. The story shows that even those who avoided theological debate would affirm the orthodox position when pressed.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical background
The passage begins with brief mentions of scholars persecuted during the mihna: al-Buwayti, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ahmad ibn Nasr. This sets the stage for why al-Muzani was cautious.
The mihna was a state-imposed inquisition that forced scholars to say the Quran is created.
2
Focus on al-Muzani's story
Read the narration from 'What clarifies this...' to '...he remained perplexed.' Notice the chain of transmission (isnad) and the dialogue.
Al-Muzani initially avoided public kalam to protect his time for fiqh.
3
Observe the key moment
When al-Muzani's students ask him directly, he confesses his belief that the Quran is uncreated. Then, when challenged by a Jahmi leader, a student volunteers to provide proofs from Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and reason.
The student's arguments leave the opponent perplexed.
4
Connect to the lesson's lesson
Why did al-Muzani refrain? He feared being forced into debates with rulers. His reluctance was not due to doubt but to protect his focus on fiqh and avoid political entanglement.
This story illustrates the practical challenges scholars faced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال البيهقى فكان كما تفرس وذلك لأنه كان شديداً على أهل البدع ذاباً بالكلام على أهل السنة ، فدعي في أيام الواثق إلى القول بخلق القرآن فامتنع منه فحمل مقيدا من مصر إلى العراق حتى مات في أقياده محبوساً ثابتاً على دينه صابراً على ما أصابه من الأذى رجمة ورضوانه عليه ، ومشهور عند أهل العلم ما أصاب أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله في أيام المعتصم من الحبس والضرب ، وما أصاب أحمد بن نصر الخزاعى فى أيام الواثق من القتل والصلب ، وما أصاب غيرهما من العظيمة حتى أجاب بعضهم إلى ما دعى إليه خوفاً على نفسه أعاذنا الله أمثالها والذى يبين هذا ما أخبرنا أبو عبد الله الحافظ قال سمعت عبد الله بن محمد الخواري يقول سمعت أبا نعيم یعنی عبد الملك بن محمد الاستراباذي يقول سمعت أبا القاسم الأنماطی یعنی عثمان بن سعيد بن المحنة [؟] فلان بشار أستاذ ابن سريج يقول جالست المزنى عشر سنين فلما كان بأخرة اجتمعنا في جنازة بعض أصحابه فقلنا يتحدثون بمذهب المزني وينسبونه إلى أنه يتكلم في القرآن ، ويقول بالمخلوق فلو سألناه قال فتقدمنا إليه فقلنا يا أبا إبراهيم إنا لنسمع منك هذا العلم ونحب أن يؤخذ عنا ما نسمع منك والناس يذكرونك أنك ساكت عن القول بما يقول أهل الحديث في القرآن ، ونحن نعلم أنك تقول بالسنة وعلى مذهب أهل الحديث فلو أظهرت لنا ما تعتقده ، فأجابنا فقال أنا لم أعتقد قط إلا أن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق ، ولكني كرهت الخوض فى هذا مخافة أن يكثر على وأطالب بالنظر فى هذا وأشتغل عن الفقه ، فلما كان من الغد بعث إليه رئيس رؤساء الجهمية يقال له ابن الأصبع رسولا ، فقال يا أبا إبراهيم بعثني إليك وهو يقول لم تزل تمسك عن الخوض في القرآن والكلام فيه ، فما الذي بدا لك الآن وقد بلغنى أنك أجبت بكذا وكذا فما حجتك فيما أجبت أن القرآن غير مخلوق ، فنظر إلينا وقال ألم أقل لكم إنى كنت أمتنع من أجل أنى أطالب بمثل هذا ، قال أبو القاسم فقلت أنا أتولى عنك جوابه ، قال شأنك فمضيت إليه فقلت له أن رسولك جاء إلى أبى إبراهيم بكذا وكذا فجئت لأتولي عنه الجواب ، وأنا أحد من تحمل عنه العلم فقال ما حجتك ، فقلت له أقول القرآن غير مخلوق وأدل عليه بكتاب الله وسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وإجماع أمته ، ومن حجج العقول التي ركبها الله في عباده قال فأوردت عليه ذلك فبقى متحيرا، قال البيهقي فالمزني رحمه الله كان رجلا ورعا زاهدا يتجنب السلاطين ، فامتنع من الكلام مخافة أن يبتلى بالدخول عليهم مع ما شاهد من محنة البويطي وأمثاله من أهل السنة ، في أيام المعتصم والواثق ، وفى كل ذلك دلالة على أن استحباب من استحب من أئمتنا ترك الخوض فى الكلام إنما هو للمعنى الذي أشرنا إليه ، وأن الكلام المذموم إنما هو كلام أهل البدع الذي يخالف الكتاب والسنة ، فأما الكلام الذي يوافق الكتاب والسنة ويبين بالعقل والعبرة فإنه محمود مرغوب فيه عند الحاجة ، تكلم فيه الشافعي وغيره من المحدثين في المناظرة إما تورعاً من أن يطأوا بساط الأمراء كما يقول الباقلاني أو لما في أنفسهم من رايق طعون المحدثين فيهم لاشتغالهم بالكلام والنظر للذب عن السنة فظنوا أنهم يعترفون بوجوب هذا العلم إذا واجهوا الامتحان بأنفسهم وخاب ظنهم ووقع ما وقع ليقضى الله أمراً كان مفعولا .
Al-Bayhaqi said: He was as he divined, and that is because he was severe against the people of innovation, defending the Sunnah with speech (kalam). He was summoned in the days of al-Wathiq to the saying that the Quran is created, and he refrained from it, so he was carried in chains from Egypt to Iraq until he died in his shackles, imprisoned, steadfast in his religion, patient upon what afflicted him of harm—Allah's mercy and pleasure be upon him. And well-known among the people of knowledge is what befell Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on him, in the days of al-Mu'tasim of imprisonment and beating, and what befell Ahmad ibn Nasr al-Khuza'i in the days of al-Wathiq of killing and crucifixion, and what befell others of great tribulation, until some of them responded to what they were called to out of fear for themselves—may Allah protect us from such things. And what clarifies this is what Abu 'Abdullah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard 'Abdullah ibn Muhammad al-Khuwari say: I heard Abu Nu'aym, meaning 'Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad al-Istrabadhi, say: I heard Abu al-Qasim al-Anmati, meaning 'Uthman ibn Sa'id ibn al-Mihna [?], say: Fulan Bishar, the teacher of Ibn Surayj, said: I sat with al-Muzani for ten years. Then when it was near the end, we gathered at a funeral of some of his companions. We said: People are talking about al-Muzani's school and attributing to him that he speaks about the Quran and says it is created. So if we asked him... He said: So we approached him and said: O Abu Ibrahim, we hear this knowledge from you and we love that what we hear from you be taken from us. People mention you that you remain silent about the saying of the people of hadith concerning the Quran. We know that you follow the Sunnah and the school of the people of hadith. So if you would show us what you believe. So he answered us and said: I have never believed anything except that the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated. But I disliked engaging in this for fear that it would increase upon me and I would be required to look into this and be occupied away from fiqh. Then the next day, a leader of the leaders of the Jahmiyya, called Ibn al-Asbagh, sent a messenger to him and said: O Abu Ibrahim, he sent me to you saying: You have continuously refrained from engaging in the Quran and speaking about it. So what has appeared to you now? For I have been informed that you answered such and such. So what is your proof in that you answered that the Quran is uncreated? So he looked at us and said: Did I not tell you that I was refraining for fear of being required with something like this? Abu al-Qasim said: I said: I will take care of his answer for you. He said: It is your business. So I went to him and said to him: Your messenger came to Abu Ibrahim concerning such and such, so I came to take care of the answer for him, and I am one of those who have transmitted knowledge from him. He said: What is your proof? So I said to him: I say the Quran is uncreated and I prove it from the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the consensus of his nation, and from rational proofs that Allah has placed in His servants. He said: So I presented that before him, and he remained perplexed. Al-Bayhaqi said: Al-Muzani, may Allah have mercy on him, was a pious, ascetic man who avoided the rulers. So he refrained from speech out of fear that he would be tested by entering upon them, considering what he witnessed of the trial of al-Buwayti and his like from the people of the Sunnah in the days of al-Mu'tasim and al-Wathiq. And in all of that is an indication that the preference of those among our imams who preferred to refrain from engaging in speech (kalam) is only for the meaning that we have pointed out, and that the blameworthy speech is only the speech of the people of innovation that contradicts the Book and the Sunnah. As for speech that agrees with the Book and the Sunnah and is clarified by reason and lesson, it is praiseworthy and desired when needed. Al-Shafi'i and others from the hadith scholars spoke in debate, either out of reluctance to tread on the carpet of the rulers, as al-Baqillani says, or because of what was in themselves of the sharp criticisms of the hadith scholars against them for their occupation with kalam and theoretical investigation for the defense of the Sunnah. So they thought that they [who refrained] would acknowledge the obligation of this knowledge when they themselves faced the trial, and their assumption failed, and what happened happened so that Allah might accomplish an affair that was to be done.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument followed by a doctrinal conclusion. Al-Bayhaqi begins by describing a scholar (likely al-Buwayti or another) who was severely persecuted for refusing to say the Quran is created, emphasizing his steadfastness. He then cites the well-known tribulations of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ahmad ibn Nasr al-Khuza'i, and others during the mihna. The main evidence for the author's thesis comes next: a narration about al-Muzani. In this story, al-Muzani is asked by his students about his belief concerning the Quran. He affirms that he believes it is uncreated but had avoided public discussion to avoid being forced into debates. When a Jahmi leader sends a messenger demanding proof, Abu al-Qasim (the narrator) volunteers and provides proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational arguments, leaving the questioner perplexed. Al-Bayhaqi then comments that al-Muzani's caution was due to his desire to avoid rulers and their trials. The key lesson is then drawn: the scholars' preference to avoid kalam was only to avoid the blameworthy kalam of the innovators. The kalam that agrees with revelation and is supported by reason and evidence is praiseworthy and even necessary when needed. Al-Bayhaqi notes that even al-Shafi'i and others engaged in such debate, and any criticism they faced stemmed from either fear of rulers or from the stigma attached by hadith scholars. The passage concludes that those who avoided kalam previously realized its necessity when they personally faced the mihna, and all unfolded by Allah's decree.

Key Terms
محنة
القرآن غير مخلوق
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Muzani avoided kalam because he doubted the Quran is uncreated or because he agreed with the Jahmis.
Correction: Al-Muzani explicitly states he never believed anything except that the Quran is uncreated; his avoidance was to protect his time for fiqh and to avoid entanglement with rulers.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Muzani initially avoid public discussion about the Quran?
A) He believed the Quran is created.
B) He feared being forced into extensive debates that would distract from fiqh.
C) He did not have any proofs.
D) He wanted to avoid the hadith scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Muzani's story shows that even scholars who avoid kalam for valid reasons firmly uphold and defend the belief that the Quran is uncreated when necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When al-Muzani said he feared being required to look into kalam and be occupied away from fiqh, is there any aspect of your religious learning that you avoid because it might distract you from your primary focus? What would it take for you to speak out like al-Muzani did when pressed?
?
The student Abu al-Qasim volunteered to defend the truth when al-Muzani was challenged. When you see someone struggling to defend the truth, do you step in, or do you wait to be asked? Reflect on a time you could have spoken but stayed silent.
?
Al-Muzani's belief was clear from the start, but he hid it for practical reasons. Are there truths about Allah you know but are afraid to voice for fear of losing something? Ask yourself: what is holding you back from declaring what you know to be true?

Defining Praiseworthy and Blameworthy Kalam
Al-Bayhaqi concludes by defining praiseworthy and blameworthy kalam based on agreement with revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between blameworthy kalam (that of innovators) and praiseworthy kalam (that agrees with Quran and Sunnah and uses reason), as articulated by al-Bayhaqi.

Core Idea
Kalam that defends the Sunnah with reason is praiseworthy; only heretical kalam is blameworthy.

After recounting the story of al-Muzani, al-Bayhaqi draws a crucial doctrinal conclusion. He explains that the early scholars' avoidance of kalam was specifically aimed at the blameworthy speech of the innovators. In contrast, engaging in theological discourse that aligns with revelation and employs rational argument is not only permissible but praiseworthy, especially when needed to defend the truth. This lesson unpacks that key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Bayhaqi's commentary on al-Muzani
Begin with the sentence 'Al-Bayhaqi said: Al-Muzani was a pious, ascetic man...' This provides context for why he avoided kalam.
Al-Muzani's fear of rulers is a key reason.
2
Identify the key distinction
Find the sentence that distinguishes blameworthy and praiseworthy kalam. It says: 'the blameworthy speech is only the speech of the people of innovation that contradicts the Book and the Sunnah. As for speech that agrees with the Book and the Sunnah and is clarified by reason and lesson, it is praiseworthy.'
This is the core thesis.
3
Understand the 'as for' construction
Notice how al-Bayhaqi first defines what is blamed, then defines what is praised. The praised category includes kalam that uses reason and lesson ('العقل والعبرة').
This shows that reason is a legitimate tool in defending the faith.
4
Consider the historical note about al-Shafi'i
Al-Bayhaqi mentions that al-Shafi'i and other hadith scholars also engaged in such kalam, but they were sometimes criticized. The reasons for their reluctance are mentioned: fear of rulers or the stigma attached by hadith scholars.
This shows that even the imams of hadith used kalam when needed.
5
Reflect on the ultimate lesson
The passage concludes that those who previously avoided kalam eventually acknowledged its necessity when they personally faced the trial. This reinforces that the ban on kalam is not absolute.
Allah's decree unfolded as it did.

قال البيهقى فكان كما تفرس وذلك لأنه كان شديداً على أهل البدع ذاباً بالكلام على أهل السنة ، فدعي في أيام الواثق إلى القول بخلق القرآن فامتنع منه فحمل مقيدا من مصر إلى العراق حتى مات في أقياده محبوساً ثابتاً على دينه صابراً على ما أصابه من الأذى رجمة ورضوانه عليه ، ومشهور عند أهل العلم ما أصاب أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله في أيام المعتصم من الحبس والضرب ، وما أصاب أحمد بن نصر الخزاعى فى أيام الواثق من فقلنا يتحدثون بمذهب المزني وينسبونه إلى أنه يتكلم في القرآن ، ويقول بالمخلوق فلو سألناه قال فتقدمنا إليه فقلنا يا أبا إبراهيم إنا لنسمع منك هذا العلم ونحب أن يؤخذ عنا ما نسمع منك والناس يذكرونك أنك ساكت عن القول بما يقول أهل الحديث في القرآن ، ونحن نعلم أنك تقول بالسنة وعلى مذهب أهل الحديث فلو أظهرت لنا ما تعتقده ، فأجابنا فقال أنا لم أعتقد قط إلا أن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق ، ولكني كرهت الخوض فى هذا مخافة أن يكثر على وأطالب بالنظر فى هذا وأشتغل عن الفقه ، فلما كان من الغد بعث إليه رئيس رؤساء الجهمية يقال له ابن الأصبع رسولا ، فقال يا أبا إبراهيم بعثني إليك وهو يقول لم تزل تمسك عن الخوض في القرآن والكلام فيه ، فما الذي بدا لك الآن وقد بلغنى أنك أجبت بكذا وكذا فما حجتك فيما أجبت أن القرآن غير مخلوق ، فنظر إلينا وقال ألم أقل لكم إنى كنت أمتنع من أجل أنى أطالب بمثل هذا ، قال أبو القاسم فقلت أنا أتولى عنك جوابه ، قال شأنك فمضيت إليه فقلت له أن رسولك جاء إلى أبى إبراهيم بكذا وكذا فجئت لأتولي عنه الجواب ، وأنا أحد من تحمل عنه العلم فقال ما حجتك ، فقلت له أقول القرآن غير مخلوق وأدل عليه بكتاب الله وسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وإجماع أمته ، ومن حجج العقول التي ركبها الله في عباده قال فأوردت عليه ذلك فبقى متحيرا، قال البيهقي فالمزني رحمه الله كان رجلا ورعا زاهدا يتجنب السلاطين ، فامتنع من الكلام مخافة أن يبتلى بالدخول عليهم مع ما شاهد من محنة البويطي وأمثاله من أهل السنة ، في أيام المعتصم والواثق ، وفى كل ذلك دلالة على أن استحباب من استحب من أئمتنا ترك الخوض فى الكلام إنما هو للمعنى الذي أشرنا إليه ، وأن الكلام المذموم إنما هو كلام أهل البدع الذي يخالف الكتاب والسنة ، فأما الكلام الذي يوافق الكتاب والسنة ويبين بالعقل والعبرة فإنه محمود مرغوب فيه عند الحاجة ، تكلم فيه الشافعي وغيره من المحدثين في المناظرة إما تورعاً من أن يطأوا بساط الأمراء كما يقول الباقلاني أو لما في أنفسهم من رايق طعون المحدثين فيهم لاشتغالهم بالكلام والنظر للذب عن السنة فظنوا أنهم يعترفون بوجوب هذا العلم إذا واجهوا الامتحان بأنفسهم وخاب ظنهم ووقع ما وقع ليقضى الله أمراً كان مفعولا .
Al-Bayhaqi said: He was as he divined, and that is because he was severe against the people of innovation, defending the Sunnah with speech (kalam). He was summoned in the days of al-Wathiq to the saying that the Quran is created, and he refrained from it, so he was carried in chains from Egypt to Iraq until he died in his shackles, imprisoned, steadfast in his religion, patient upon what afflicted him of harm—Allah's mercy and pleasure be upon him. And well-known among the people of knowledge is what befell Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on him, in the days of al-Mu'tasim of imprisonment and beating, and what befell Ahmad ibn Nasr al-Khuza'i in the days of al-Wathiq of killing and crucifixion, and what befell others of great tribulation, until some of them responded to what they were called to out of fear for themselves—may Allah protect us from such things. And what clarifies this is what Abu 'Abdullah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard 'Abdullah ibn Muhammad al-Khuwari say: I heard Abu Nu'aym, meaning 'Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad al-Istrabadhi, say: I heard Abu al-Qasim al-Anmati, meaning 'Uthman ibn Sa'id ibn al-Mihna [?], say: Fulan Bishar, the teacher of Ibn Surayj, said: I sat with al-Muzani for ten years. Then when it was near the end, we gathered at a funeral of some of his companions. We said: People are talking about al-Muzani's school and attributing to him that he speaks about the Quran and says it is created. So if we asked him... He said: So we approached him and said: O Abu Ibrahim, we hear this knowledge from you and we love that what we hear from you be taken from us. People mention you that you remain silent about the saying of the people of hadith concerning the Quran. We know that you follow the Sunnah and the school of the people of hadith. So if you would show us what you believe. So he answered us and said: I have never believed anything except that the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated. But I disliked engaging in this for fear that it would increase upon me and I would be required to look into this and be occupied away from fiqh. Then the next day, a leader of the leaders of the Jahmiyya, called Ibn al-Asbagh, sent a messenger to him and said: O Abu Ibrahim, he sent me to you saying: You have continuously refrained from engaging in the Quran and speaking about it. So what has appeared to you now? For I have been informed that you answered such and such. So what is your proof in that you answered that the Quran is uncreated? So he looked at us and said: Did I not tell you that I was refraining for fear of being required with something like this? Abu al-Qasim said: I said: I will take care of his answer for you. He said: It is your business. So I went to him and said to him: Your messenger came to Abu Ibrahim concerning such and such, so I came to take care of the answer for him, and I am one of those who have transmitted knowledge from him. He said: What is your proof? So I said to him: I say the Quran is uncreated and I prove it from the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the consensus of his nation, and from rational proofs that Allah has placed in His servants. He said: So I presented that before him, and he remained perplexed. Al-Bayhaqi said: Al-Muzani, may Allah have mercy on him, was a pious, ascetic man who avoided the rulers. So he refrained from speech out of fear that he would be tested by entering upon them, considering what he witnessed of the trial of al-Buwayti and his like from the people of the Sunnah in the days of al-Mu'tasim and al-Wathiq. And in all of that is an indication that the preference of those among our imams who preferred to refrain from engaging in speech (kalam) is only for the meaning that we have pointed out, and that the blameworthy speech is only the speech of the people of innovation that contradicts the Book and the Sunnah. As for speech that agrees with the Book and the Sunnah and is clarified by reason and lesson, it is praiseworthy and desired when needed. Al-Shafi'i and others from the hadith scholars spoke in debate, either out of reluctance to tread on the carpet of the rulers, as al-Baqillani says, or because of what was in themselves of the sharp criticisms of the hadith scholars against them for their occupation with kalam and theoretical investigation for the defense of the Sunnah. So they thought that they [who refrained] would acknowledge the obligation of this knowledge when they themselves faced the trial, and their assumption failed, and what happened happened so that Allah might accomplish an affair that was to be done.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument followed by a doctrinal conclusion. Al-Bayhaqi begins by describing a scholar (likely al-Buwayti or another) who was severely persecuted for refusing to say the Quran is created, emphasizing his steadfastness. He then cites the well-known tribulations of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ahmad ibn Nasr al-Khuza'i, and others during the mihna. The main evidence for the author's thesis comes next: a narration about al-Muzani. In this story, al-Muzani is asked by his students about his belief concerning the Quran. He affirms that he believes it is uncreated but had avoided public discussion to avoid being forced into debates. When a Jahmi leader sends a messenger demanding proof, Abu al-Qasim (the narrator) volunteers and provides proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational arguments, leaving the questioner perplexed. Al-Bayhaqi then comments that al-Muzani's caution was due to his desire to avoid rulers and their trials. The key lesson is then drawn: the scholars' preference to avoid kalam was only to avoid the blameworthy kalam of the innovators. The kalam that agrees with revelation and is supported by reason and evidence is praiseworthy and even necessary when needed. Al-Bayhaqi notes that even al-Shafi'i and others engaged in such debate, and any criticism they faced stemmed from either fear of rulers or from the stigma attached by hadith scholars. The passage concludes that those who avoided kalam previously realized its necessity when they personally faced the mihna, and all unfolded by Allah's decree.

Key Terms
كلام مذموم
كلام محمود
العقل والعبرة
الكتاب والسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all forms of kalam (theological discourse) are forbidden or blameworthy.
Correction: Al-Bayhaqi clarifies that only the kalam of innovators that contradicts revelation is blameworthy; kalam that supports the Sunnah and uses reason is praiseworthy and encouraged when needed.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi, what is the criterion for praiseworthy kalam?
A) It must be spoken in private.
B) It must agree with the Quran and Sunnah and be clarified by reason and lesson.
C) It must be based solely on reason.
D) It must avoid any mention of the Quran's creation.

Key Takeaway
Praiseworthy kalam is that which defends the Sunnah using rational arguments in conformity with the Quran and Sunnah; it is not only allowed but commendable when necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely avoided deep theological study because you thought it was all 'kalam'—something to be feared or avoided. After reading this passage, what is your accountability before Allah for neglecting the praiseworthy kalam that defends the Sunnah? What specific step will you take this week to learn the rational proofs for your creed?
?
When a skeptic or innovator challenges your faith, will your silence be excused by 'avoiding kalam'? Or does this passage condemn your complacency? Commit to one concrete action to prepare yourself to defend the Sunnah when the need arises.
?
Al-Muzani feared rulers; what authorities or people do you fear that prevent you from speaking the truth? Is your fear of creation greater than your fear of Allah? How will you repent from this silence today?

Sects and Disagreements

The Refutation of Limiting Madhhabs to Four
The author refutes the claim that only four madhhabs exist by listing many other scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of the claim that only four madhhabs exist, and the evidence he provides by listing many other scholars.

Core Idea
The number of Islamic legal schools is not limited to four; many others existed.

In this passage, Imam Ibn 'Asakir responds to the objection that the Ash'aris have invented a fifth madhhab. He refutes this by pointing out that the objector has no authority to limit the number of schools, and then lists numerous scholars who had their own schools, emphasizing that their differences were in subsidiary rulings, not in fundamentals.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the opening statement of the ignorant innovators who claim only four madhhabs exist and accuse the Ash'aris of inventing a fifth.
Notice the tone: they are dismissive and claim not to recognize other schools.
2
Read the refutation
The author refutes by questioning their authority to limit the number and stating that most schools are not limited to four.
The refutation is direct and firm.
3
Identify the listed scholars
The author lists several scholars as examples: al-Layth, al-Batti, Ishaq, Dawud, and others like Sufyan al-Thawri, Abu 'Ubayd, etc.
These scholars had their own schools and were well-known.
4
Note the distinction
The author emphasizes that these scholars differed in legal rulings (furu') not in fundamentals of religion (usul).
This is key to understanding the nature of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال بعض الجهال المبتدعة لسنا نعرف غير المذاهب الأربعة فمن أين أتى هذا المذهب الخامس الذي أختر عتموه ولم رضيتم لانفسكم بالانتساب إلى الأشعري الذي أتبعتموه وهلا أقتنعتم بالانتساب إلى الامام الألمعي أبي عبد الله محمد بن إدريس الشافعي فإنه أولى بالانتساب إليه ممن سواه وأحق بالانتماء إلى مذهبه ممن عداه ؟ قلنا هذا قول عرى عن الصدق وقائله بعيد عن الحق فمن ذا الذي حصر المذاهب بالعدد الذي حصرتم ومن يصحح لكم من قولكم ما ذكرتم ، بل المذاهب أكثرها لا ينحصر بهذا العدد الذى عددتم ولو كانت منحصرة به لم يحصل لكم بذلك ما قصدتم وكأنكم لم تسمعوا بمذهب الليث بن سعد المصرى وعثمان بن سليمان البتى البصرى وإسحق بن راهويه . الخراسانی و داود ابن على الأصبهاني وغيرهم (۱) من علماء الإسلام الذين اختلفوا في الفتاوى والأحكام لا فى أصول الدين المبنية على القطع واليقين (۱) كسفيان الثوري وأبي عبيد وأبي ثور وابن جرير وغيرهم . أما الليث فهو أصبهاني الأصل فارسى النسب مصرى الدار والوفاة كان غنياً كبيراً يواسى أهل العلم والزهاد ولم تجب عليه زكاة مع كثرة دخله وكان إذا خرج إلى الحج خرج بثلاث سفن سفينة لنفسه وعائلته وثانية لضيوفه وثالثه لخدمه وطباخيه وأزواده ، تفقه على ربيعة وأبي حنيفة وجمع بين الطريقتين الحجازية والعراقية فى الفقه وكان الشافعي يقدمه على مالك وللناس في إطرائ، كلمات ولكن لم يقم أصحابه بعلمه حق القيام ولم يكن له مسائل انفرد بها في الفقه ولعل هذا من أسباب الاستغناء عن تدوين مذهبه وجزم القاضي زكريا الانصاري في شرح البخاري أنه حنفى ونقل ابن خلكان فى وفياته مثل ذلك عن مجموعة وذكر ابن أبي العوام قبلهما أنه ممن أخذ عن أبي حنيفة . والحق أنه استقل فى الاجتهاد وله رسالة وجهها إلى مالك - يجيب فيها عما أورده مالك فى رسالة كان بعثها إليه - تدل على غزارة علمه وكبر محله في الاجتهاد وقد ذكرنا كلتا الرسالتين القيمتين بنصيهما في كتابنا ( قطرات الغيث من حياة الإمام الليث ( لعظم فائدتهما لمن يعني بتاريخ الفقه الإسلامي وكيفية تطوره . وأما عثمان البتى فهو فقيه البصرة في عهد أبي حنيفة وأقدم الأئمة وفاة واختلفوا في اسم أبيه قبل مسلم بن جرموز وعليه ألا كثرون وقيل سليمان كما هنا وقيل أسلم . تفقه على الحسن البصرى وأصحابه وهو كثير الشذوذ في الفقه ومات مذهبه قبل أن يولد بمناظرات زفر معه في رحلته الأولى إلى البصرة ومواصلته النقض في رحلته الأخيرة . وفيه كان يقول أبو حنيفة : ( لو رآني البتي لأخذ بكثير من أقوالي ، وقد تصحف بالنبي على مثل من يجعل ( عن الله عز وجل ) ( عن الله عن رجل ( فذكره في مثالبه ، قال ابن حجر في : اللسان ) رواية عن طريق أحمد بن عبدة الضبي : قدم زفر بن الهذيل البصرة فكان يأتي حلقة عثمان البتى فيناظرهم ويتبع أصولهم ويسألهم عن فروعهم فإذا رأى شيئاً خرجوا فيه عن الأصل تكلم فيه مع عثمان حتى يتبين له خروجه من الأصل ثم يقول : فى هذا جواب أحسن من هذا فإذا استحسنوه قال هذا قول أبي حنيفة فلم يلبث أن تحولت الحلقة إليه وبقى عثمان البتى وحده أهـ . وأما إسحق فقد كان تفقه على مذهب أهل العراق بخراسان واستخرج من كتب ابن المبارك ما يوافق رأى أبي حنيفة من الأحاديث قبلغت نحواً من ثلثمائة حديث ولما رحل إلى العراق ما كان يظن أن أحداً يجترئ أن يخالف أبا حنيفة كما حكى هو عن نفسه على ما في كتاب ( الورع ، رواية أبي بكر المروزى ولما قدم البصرة جلس إلى عبد الرحمن بن مهدى فأماله إلى الرواية وحين قام سوق الرواية استقل بمذهب لكن لم يعش . وأما داود فقد تفقه على أبي ثور ثم نفى القياس قال ابن أبي حاتم : ألف على ذلك كتباً في الفقه شذ فيها عن السلف وابتدع طريقة هجره أكثر أهل العلم عليها .. ورأيه أضعف الأراء وأبعدها من طريق الفقه وأكثرها شذوذاً أهـ . قال أبو حاتم لا يلتفت إلى وساوسه وخطراته . وليس انقراض أرباب هذه المذاهب التي سمينا يصحح لهذا الجاهل هذه المقالة التي عنه حكينا
If some ignorant innovators say: 'We do not know any other than the four schools; where did this fifth school come from that you invented? And why are you satisfied with attributing yourselves to al-Ash'ari whom you follow? Why were you not content to attribute yourselves to the brilliant imam Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, for he is more deserving of attribution than others and more worthy of following his school than others?' We say: This statement is stripped of truth and its speaker is far from truth. For who has confined the schools to the number you have confined? And who can validate for you what you mentioned? Rather, most schools are not limited to this number you counted, and even if they were limited to it, you would not attain what you intended. It is as if you have not heard of the school of al-Layth ibn Sa'd al-Misri, 'Uthman ibn Sulayman al-Batti al-Basri, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh al-Khurasani, Dawud ibn 'Ali al-Isfahani, and others among the scholars of Islam who differed in legal opinions and rulings, not in the fundamentals of religion based on certainty. (1) Like Sufyan al-Thawri, Abu 'Ubayd, Abu Thawr, Ibn Jarir, and others. As for al-Layth: he was of Isfahani origin, Persian lineage, Egyptian residence and death. He was very wealthy, supporting the people of knowledge and ascetics, and zakah was not obligatory upon him despite his abundant income. When he went for hajj, he went with three ships: one for himself and his family, a second for his guests, and a third for his servants, cooks, and supplies. He studied fiqh under Rabi'ah and Abu Hanifah, combining the Hijazi and Iraqi methods in fiqh. Al-Shafi'i preferred him over Malik. People have words of praise for him, but his students did not fully uphold his knowledge, and he had no rulings exclusive to himself in fiqh. Perhaps this is among the reasons for dispensing with recording his school. Qadi Zakariyya al-Ansari affirmed in his commentary on al-Bukhari that he was Hanafi, and Ibn Khallikan in his Deaths reported likewise from a collection, and Ibn Abi al-'Awwam before them said he was among those who took from Abu Hanifah. The truth is that he was independent in ijtihad, and he had a letter sent to Malik responding to what Malik had raised in a letter he had sent to him, indicating his abundant knowledge and high standing in ijtihad. We have mentioned both valuable letters in full in our book 'Qatarat al-Ghayth min Hayat al-Imam al-Layth' because of their great benefit for those interested in the history of Islamic fiqh and its development. As for 'Uthman al-Batti: he was the mufti of Basra in the era of Abu Hanifah and the earliest of the imams in death. They differed concerning his father's name: before Muslim ibn Jarmuz, and the majority say it is Muslim, and it is said Sulayman as here, and it is said Aslam. He studied fiqh under al-Hasan al-Basri and his companions, and he had much irregularity in fiqh. His school died before he was born because of the debates of Zufar with him on his first journey to Basra and his continuous refutation on his last journey. About him, Abu Hanifah used to say: 'If al-Batti had seen me, he would have adopted many of my statements.' And it (the name) was corrupted to 'al-Nabi' by someone who makes [؟] about [؟]. Ibn Hajar in al-Lisan narrated via Ahmad ibn 'Abdat al-Dabbi: 'Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl came to Basra and used to attend the circle of 'Uthman al-Batti, debating them, following their principles, and asking them about their branches. When he saw something in which they deviated from the principle, he would discuss it with 'Uthman until he made clear his deviation from the principle, then he would say: 'There is a better answer than this.' When they approved it, he would say: 'This is the statement of Abu Hanifah.' It was not long before the circle turned to him, and 'Uthman al-Batti remained alone.' End quote. As for Ishaq: he studied fiqh according to the Iraqi school in Khurasan and extracted from the books of Ibn al-Mubarak about three hundred hadith that agreed with the opinion of Abu Hanifah. When he traveled to Iraq, he thought that no one would dare oppose Abu Hanifah, as he himself related, according to the book 'al-Wara'' narrated by Abu Bakr al-Marwazi. When he came to Basra, he sat with 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, who swayed him toward narration. When the market of narration flourished, he became independent with a school, but he did not live long. As for Dawud: he studied fiqh under Abu Thawr, then denied qiyas. Ibn Abi Hatim said: 'He authored books on fiqh on that basis, in which he deviated from the salaf and innovated a method that most scholars abandoned him for... His opinion is the weakest of opinions, the farthest from the path of fiqh, and the most irregular.' End quote. Abu Hatim said: 'Do not pay attention to his whisperings and thoughts.' And the extinction of the adherents of these schools that we have mentioned does not validate for this ignorant one the statement we have related from him.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The author first presents the objection of some ignoramus innovators who claim that only four madhhabs exist and accuse the Ash'aris of inventing a fifth madhhab, suggesting they should instead attribute themselves to al-Shafi'i. The author refutes this by stating the objection is false and that the objector has no authority to limit the number of madhhabs. He then lists many other scholars who had their own madhhabs, including al-Layth ibn Sa'd, 'Uthman al-Batti, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Dawud al-Isfahani, and others, emphasizing that they differed only in legal rulings, not in fundamentals of religion. The author then provides detailed biographical notes on each of these scholars, highlighting their contributions, the fate of their schools, and how some did not survive due to various reasons. Finally, he concludes that the extinction of these schools does not justify the objector's claim that only four madhhabs exist.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only four madhhabs exist in Islam.
Correction: Many other scholars had their own madhhabs, as evidenced by the list provided.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinction does the author make about the scholars he lists?
A) They all followed the same school.
B) They differed in legal rulings but not in fundamentals of religion.
C) They were all from the same region.
D) They all rejected analogy.

Key Takeaway
The existence of many scholars with their own madhhabs proves that Islamic legal schools are not limited to four.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a position or school of thought simply because it was unfamiliar, without investigating its scholarly basis? Will you commit to seeking knowledge before judging others?
?
Do you tend to elevate one scholar or madhhab to the point of denying the legitimacy of others? How can you guard against this while still respecting your own school?
?
If you were asked to defend why you follow a particular madhhab or theological school, could you do so without disrespecting others? What step will you take this week to learn about a different valid scholarly opinion?

Biographical Proofs: The Existence of Other Madhhabs
The author provides detailed biographies of four scholars to demonstrate the existence of their madhhabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn about four scholars—al-Layth, al-Batti, Ishaq, and Dawud—whose schools did not survive but demonstrate the existence of more than four madhhabs.

Core Idea
These four scholars had their own schools, proving that more than four madhhabs existed.

In this passage, Imam Ibn 'Asakir provides detailed biographies of four scholars—al-Layth ibn Sa'd, 'Uthman al-Batti, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and Dawud al-Isfahani—to further support his refutation. He explains their scholarship, the fate of their schools, and why they did not survive.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography of al-Layth ibn Sa'd
Learn about his wealth, his combination of Hijazi and Iraqi methods in fiqh, and why his school did not survive despite his high standing.
Note that al-Shafi'i preferred him over Malik.
2
Read the biography of 'Uthman al-Batti
Understand his role as mufti of Basra, his many irregular opinions, and how his school died out due to debates with Zufar.
Abu Hanifah said about him: 'If al-Batti had seen me, he would have adopted many of my statements.'
3
Read the biography of Ishaq ibn Rahawayh
He studied the Iraqi school and extracted hadith supporting Abu Hanifah, but he was swayed by 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi towards narration and his school did not last.
He thought no one would oppose Abu Hanifah.
4
Read the biography of Dawud al-Isfahani
He studied under Abu Thawr, then denied qiyas and innovated a method that was abandoned by most scholars.
His opinion is described as the weakest and most irregular.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that the extinction of these schools does not validate the objector's claim that only four madhhabs exist.
The biographical details serve as evidence that these schools did exist.

فإن قال بعض الجهال المبتدعة لسنا نعرف غير المذاهب الأربعة فمن أين أتى هذا المذهب الخامس الذي أختر عتموه ولم رضيتم لانفسكم بالانتساب إلى الأشعري الذي أتبعتموه وهلا أقتنعتم بالانتساب إلى الامام الألمعي أبي عبد الله محمد بن إدريس الشافعي فإنه أولى بالانتساب إليه ممن سواه وأحق بالانتماء إلى مذهبه ممن عداه ؟ قلنا هذا قول عرى عن الصدق وقائله بعيد عن الحق فمن ذا الذي حصر المذاهب بالعدد الذي حصرتم ومن يصحح لكم من قولكم ما ذكرتم ، بل المذاهب أكثرها لا ينحصر بهذا العدد الذى عددتم ولو كانت منحصرة به لم يحصل لكم بذلك ما قصدتم وكأنكم لم تسمعوا بمذهب الليث بن سعد المصرى وعثمان بن سليمان البتى البصرى وإسحق بن راهويه . الخراسانی و داود ابن على الأصبهاني وغيرهم (۱) من علماء الإسلام الذين اختلفوا في الفتاوى والأحكام لا فى أصول الدين المبنية على القطع واليقين (۱) كسفيان الثوري وأبي عبيد وأبي ثور وابن جرير وغيرهم . أما الليث فهو أصبهاني الأصل فارسى النسب مصرى الدار والوفاة كان غنياً كبيراً يواسى أهل العلم والزهاد ولم تجب عليه زكاة مع كثرة دخله وكان إذا خرج إلى الحج خرج بثلاث سفن سفينة لنفسه وعائلته وثانية لضيوفه وثالثه لخدمه وطباخيه وأزواده ، تفقه على ربيعة وأبي حنيفة وجمع بين الطريقتين الحجازية والعراقية فى الفقه وكان الشافعي يقدمه على مالك وللناس في إطرائ، كلمات ولكن لم يقم أصحابه بعلمه حق القيام ولم يكن له مسائل انفرد بها في الفقه ولعل هذا من أسباب الاستغناء عن تدوين مذهبه وجزم القاضي زكريا الانصاري في شرح البخاري أنه حنفى ونقل ابن خلكان فى وفياته مثل ذلك عن مجموعة وذكر ابن أبي العوام قبلهما أنه ممن أخذ عن أبي حنيفة . والحق أنه استقل فى الاجتهاد وله رسالة وجهها إلى مالك - يجيب فيها عما أورده مالك فى رسالة كان بعثها إليه - تدل على غزارة علمه وكبر محله في الاجتهاد وقد ذكرنا كلتا الرسالتين القيمتين بنصيهما في كتابنا ( قطرات الغيث من حياة الإمام الليث ( لعظم فائدتهما لمن يعني بتاريخ الفقه الإسلامي وكيفية تطوره . وأما عثمان البتى فهو فقيه البصرة في عهد أبي حنيفة وأقدم الأئمة وفاة واختلفوا في اسم أبيه قبل مسلم بن جرموز وعليه ألا كثرون وقيل سليمان كما هنا وقيل أسلم . تفقه على الحسن البصرى وأصحابه وهو كثير الشذوذ في الفقه ومات مذهبه قبل أن يولد بمناظرات زفر معه في رحلته الأولى إلى البصرة ومواصلته النقض في رحلته الأخيرة . وفيه كان يقول أبو حنيفة : ( لو رآني البتي لأخذ بكثير من أقوالي ، وقد تصحف بالنبي على مثل من يجعل ( عن الله عز وجل ) ( عن الله عن رجل ( فذكره في مثالبه ، قال ابن حجر في : اللسان ) رواية عن طريق أحمد بن عبدة الضبي : قدم زفر بن الهذيل البصرة فكان يأتي حلقة عثمان البتى فيناظرهم ويتبع أصولهم ويسألهم عن فروعهم فإذا رأى شيئاً خرجوا فيه عن الأصل تكلم فيه مع عثمان حتى يتبين له خروجه من الأصل ثم يقول : فى هذا جواب أحسن من هذا فإذا استحسنوه قال هذا قول أبي حنيفة فلم يلبث أن تحولت الحلقة إليه وبقى عثمان البتى وحده أهـ . وأما إسحق فقد كان تفقه على مذهب أهل العراق بخراسان واستخرج من كتب ابن المبارك ما يوافق رأى أبي حنيفة من الأحاديث قبلغت نحواً من ثلثمائة حديث ولما رحل إلى العراق ما كان يظن أن أحداً يجترئ أن يخالف أبا حنيفة كما حكى هو عن نفسه على ما في كتاب ( الورع ، رواية أبي بكر المروزى ولما قدم البصرة جلس إلى عبد الرحمن بن مهدى فأماله إلى الرواية وحين قام سوق الرواية استقل بمذهب لكن لم يعش . وأما داود فقد تفقه على أبي ثور ثم نفى القياس قال ابن أبي حاتم : ألف على ذلك كتباً في الفقه شذ فيها عن السلف وابتدع طريقة هجره أكثر أهل العلم عليها .. ورأيه أضعف الأراء وأبعدها من طريق الفقه وأكثرها شذوذاً أهـ . قال أبو حاتم لا يلتفت إلى وساوسه وخطراته . وليس انقراض أرباب هذه المذاهب التي سمينا يصحح لهذا الجاهل هذه المقالة التي عنه حكينا
If some ignorant innovators say: 'We do not know any other than the four schools; where did this fifth school come from that you invented? And why are you satisfied with attributing yourselves to al-Ash'ari whom you follow? Why were you not content to attribute yourselves to the brilliant imam Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, for he is more deserving of attribution than others and more worthy of following his school than others?' We say: This statement is stripped of truth and its speaker is far from truth. For who has confined the schools to the number you have confined? And who can validate for you what you mentioned? Rather, most schools are not limited to this number you counted, and even if they were limited to it, you would not attain what you intended. It is as if you have not heard of the school of al-Layth ibn Sa'd al-Misri, 'Uthman ibn Sulayman al-Batti al-Basri, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh al-Khurasani, Dawud ibn 'Ali al-Isfahani, and others among the scholars of Islam who differed in legal opinions and rulings, not in the fundamentals of religion based on certainty. (1) Like Sufyan al-Thawri, Abu 'Ubayd, Abu Thawr, Ibn Jarir, and others. As for al-Layth: he was of Isfahani origin, Persian lineage, Egyptian residence and death. He was very wealthy, supporting the people of knowledge and ascetics, and zakah was not obligatory upon him despite his abundant income. When he went for hajj, he went with three ships: one for himself and his family, a second for his guests, and a third for his servants, cooks, and supplies. He studied fiqh under Rabi'ah and Abu Hanifah, combining the Hijazi and Iraqi methods in fiqh. Al-Shafi'i preferred him over Malik. People have words of praise for him, but his students did not fully uphold his knowledge, and he had no rulings exclusive to himself in fiqh. Perhaps this is among the reasons for dispensing with recording his school. Qadi Zakariyya al-Ansari affirmed in his commentary on al-Bukhari that he was Hanafi, and Ibn Khallikan in his Deaths reported likewise from a collection, and Ibn Abi al-'Awwam before them said he was among those who took from Abu Hanifah. The truth is that he was independent in ijtihad, and he had a letter sent to Malik responding to what Malik had raised in a letter he had sent to him, indicating his abundant knowledge and high standing in ijtihad. We have mentioned both valuable letters in full in our book 'Qatarat al-Ghayth min Hayat al-Imam al-Layth' because of their great benefit for those interested in the history of Islamic fiqh and its development. As for 'Uthman al-Batti: he was the mufti of Basra in the era of Abu Hanifah and the earliest of the imams in death. They differed concerning his father's name: before Muslim ibn Jarmuz, and the majority say it is Muslim, and it is said Sulayman as here, and it is said Aslam. He studied fiqh under al-Hasan al-Basri and his companions, and he had much irregularity in fiqh. His school died before he was born because of the debates of Zufar with him on his first journey to Basra and his continuous refutation on his last journey. About him, Abu Hanifah used to say: 'If al-Batti had seen me, he would have adopted many of my statements.' And it (the name) was corrupted to 'al-Nabi' by someone who makes [؟] about [؟]. Ibn Hajar in al-Lisan narrated via Ahmad ibn 'Abdat al-Dabbi: 'Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl came to Basra and used to attend the circle of 'Uthman al-Batti, debating them, following their principles, and asking them about their branches. When he saw something in which they deviated from the principle, he would discuss it with 'Uthman until he made clear his deviation from the principle, then he would say: 'There is a better answer than this.' When they approved it, he would say: 'This is the statement of Abu Hanifah.' It was not long before the circle turned to him, and 'Uthman al-Batti remained alone.' End quote. As for Ishaq: he studied fiqh according to the Iraqi school in Khurasan and extracted from the books of Ibn al-Mubarak about three hundred hadith that agreed with the opinion of Abu Hanifah. When he traveled to Iraq, he thought that no one would dare oppose Abu Hanifah, as he himself related, according to the book 'al-Wara'' narrated by Abu Bakr al-Marwazi. When he came to Basra, he sat with 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, who swayed him toward narration. When the market of narration flourished, he became independent with a school, but he did not live long. As for Dawud: he studied fiqh under Abu Thawr, then denied qiyas. Ibn Abi Hatim said: 'He authored books on fiqh on that basis, in which he deviated from the salaf and innovated a method that most scholars abandoned him for... His opinion is the weakest of opinions, the farthest from the path of fiqh, and the most irregular.' End quote. Abu Hatim said: 'Do not pay attention to his whisperings and thoughts.' And the extinction of the adherents of these schools that we have mentioned does not validate for this ignorant one the statement we have related from him.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The author first presents the objection of some ignoramus innovators who claim that only four madhhabs exist and accuse the Ash'aris of inventing a fifth madhhab, suggesting they should instead attribute themselves to al-Shafi'i. The author refutes this by stating the objection is false and that the objector has no authority to limit the number of madhhabs. He then lists many other scholars who had their own madhhabs, including al-Layth ibn Sa'd, 'Uthman al-Batti, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Dawud al-Isfahani, and others, emphasizing that they differed only in legal rulings, not in fundamentals of religion. The author then provides detailed biographical notes on each of these scholars, highlighting their contributions, the fate of their schools, and how some did not survive due to various reasons. Finally, he concludes that the extinction of these schools does not justify the objector's claim that only four madhhabs exist.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Layth's school not survive?
A) He was not a good scholar.
B) His students did not uphold his knowledge and he had no exclusive rulings.
C) He was a Hanafi all along.
D) He died young.

Key Takeaway
The detailed biographies of al-Layth, al-Batti, Ishaq, and Dawud provide concrete evidence that many madhhabs existed beyond the famous four.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a scholar or a teaching simply because it is not well-known today? In light of this lesson, what does this reveal about your attitude toward knowledge—do you judge truth by its popularity? Take a moment to repent for any such arrogance and commit to evaluating truth based on evidence, not fame.
?
The students of al-Layth failed to preserve his school. If you were one of his students, would you have been diligent in transmitting his knowledge? What does your current effort to learn and teach Islam say about your priority for the preservation of truth? Write down one concrete step you will take this week to ensure you are preserving what you learn.
?
The school of al-Batti vanished because his followers were won over by Zufar's arguments. Have you ever abandoned a correct position because someone with more eloquence or confidence persuaded you? Ask yourself: Are you easily swayed by charismatic speakers, or do you anchor yourself in solid evidence from the Quran and Sunnah? Resolve to study the proofs behind what you believe.

The Ash'ari School: Continuation of Sunni Theology
The author clarifies that Ash'ari revived Sunni theology and that his followers rely on evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Ash'ari school is not a new innovation but a revival of Sunni orthodoxy, grounded in evidence and in agreement with the four imams on tawhid and tanzih.

Core Idea
Ash'ari revived Sunni theology, not invented a fifth school; his followers rely on evidence, not blind imitation.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari defends the Ash'ari school against accusations that it represents a fifth madhhab. The author explains that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari only revived the teachings of Ahl al-Sunnah that had been obscured by innovators. He then clarifies that Ash'aris do not blindly follow but agree based on proofs, and that the four imams are united on the fundamentals of tawhid and transcendence. The passage concludes with a powerful statement: if affirming transcendence is called Ash'arism, then all monotheists are Ash'aris.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Pay attention to the author's defensive tone.
The passage is a continuous argument; read it as a whole.
2
Identify the key claims
What does the author deny (Ash'ari invented a fifth school) and affirm (he revived Sunni teachings)?
3
Note the list of deviant sects
The author lists Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Mujassima, etc. Why are they mentioned?
They are the groups Ash'ari refuted.
4
Understand the relationship with the four imams
How does the author view the four imams? Are they in disagreement on fundamentals?
The author asserts they are united on tawhid and tanzih.
5
Reflect on the final statement
What does it mean to say 'all monotheists are Ash'aris'?
It collapses the label into the core belief.

ولسنا نسلم أن أبا الحسن اخترع مذهباً خامسا وإنما أقام من مذاهب أهل السنة ما صار عند المبتدعة دارسا وأوضح من أقوال من تقدمه من الأربعة وغيرهم ما غدا ملتبسا وجدد من معالم الشريعة ما أصبح بتكذيب من اعتدى منطمسا ولسنا ننتسب بمذهبنا في التوحيد إليه على معنى أنا نقلده فيه ونعتمد عليه ولكنا نوافقه على ما صار إليه من التوحيد لقيام الأدلة على صحته لا لمجرد التقليد وإنما ينتسب منا من انتسب إلى مذهبه ليتميز عن المبتدعة الذين لا يقولون به من أصناف المعتزلة والجهمية المعطلة والمجسمة والكرامية والمشبهة السالمية وغيرهم من سائر طوائف المبتدعة وأصحاب المقالات الفاسدة المخترعة لأن الأشعرى هو الذى انتدب للرد عليهم حتى قمعهم وأظهر لمن لم يعرف البدع بدعهم ولسنا نرى الأئمة الأربعة الذين عنيـتـم في أصول الدين مختلفين ، بل نراهم في القول بتوحيد الله وتنزيهه في ذاته مؤتلفين وعلى نفى التشبيه عن القديم سبحانه وتعالى مجتمعين ، والأشعري رحمه الله في الاصول علي منهاجهم أجمعين ، فما علي من انتسب إليه على هذا الوجه جناح ولا يرجى لمن تبرأ من عقيدته الصحيحة فلاح ، فإن عددتم القول بالتنزيه وترك التشبيه تمشعرا فالموحدون بأسرهم أشعرية ولا يضر عصابة انتمت إلى موحد مجرد التشنيع عليها بما هى منه برية ، وهذا كقول إمامنا الشافعي المطلبي ابن عم المصطفى النبي صلي الله عليه وسلم فيما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن عبد الله بن أحمد الواسطى ببغداد ، قال أنا
And we do not concede that Abu al-Hasan invented a fifth school. Rather, he revived from the schools of Ahl al-Sunnah what had become obsolete among the innovators, and clarified from the statements of those before him among the Four and others what had become ambiguous, and renewed from the landmarks of the Shari'ah what had become obliterated by the denial of the transgressors. And we do not attribute ourselves in our school of tawhid to him in the sense that we blindly follow him and rely on him. Rather, we agree with him on what he arrived at concerning tawhid because of the establishment of proofs for its correctness, not for mere imitation. Rather, whoever among us attributes himself to his school does so to distinguish himself from the innovators who do not adhere to it—from the categories of the Mu'tazila, the Jahmiyya Mu'atila, the Mujassima, the Karramiyya, the Mushabbiha al-Salimiyya, and others from the rest of the sects of innovators and people of false invented opinions. Because al-Ash'ari is the one who devoted himself to refuting them until he suppressed them and showed to those who did not know innovation their innovations. And we do not see the four imams that you mentioned differing in the fundamentals of religion. Rather, we see them in affirming the oneness of Allah and declaring His transcendence in His essence united, and upon negating anthropomorphism from the Eternal, glorified and exalted, agreed. And al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him, in the fundamentals is upon their path all. So there is no sin upon whoever attributes himself to him in this manner, nor is success hoped for whoever disavows his correct creed. For if you call the affirmation of transcendence and abandonment of anthropomorphism 'Ash'arism,' then all monotheists are Ash'aris. And mere vilification does not harm a group that has aligned itself with a monotheist, for they are innocent of it. And this is like the statement of our imam al-Shafi'i, the Muttalibi, the cousin of the Chosen Prophet, peace be upon him, as narrated to us by Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibatullah ibn 'Abdillah ibn Ahmad al-Wasiti in Baghdad: he said, 'I...'
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of the nature of the Ash'ari school. The author refutes the claim that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari invented a fifth madhhab, explaining instead that he revived the teachings of Ahl al-Sunnah that had become neglected by innovators. He emphasizes that followers of Ash'ari do not blindly imitate him but agree based on evidence. They attribute themselves to his school to distinguish themselves from various innovated sects (Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Mujassima, etc.), because Ash'ari devoted himself to refuting these groups. The author then asserts that the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) are not in disagreement on the fundamentals of tawhid and tanzih; they are united on negating anthropomorphism. Ash'ari follows their path. Therefore, attributing oneself to Ash'ari in this sense is blameless. Indeed, if affirming transcendence and rejecting anthropomorphism is called Ash'arism, then all monotheists are Ash'aris. The author concludes with a quote from Imam al-Shafi'i (though the quote is cut off).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari invented a fifth madhhab and his followers blindly imitate him.
Correction: Ash'ari revived Sunni teachings that had become obsolete; his followers agree based on proofs, not mere imitation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why do followers of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari attribute themselves to him?
A) Because they blindly imitate him in all matters.
B) To distinguish themselves from the four imams.
C) To distinguish themselves from various innovated sects and because they agree with him based on proof.
D) Because he invented a new fifth school.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school is a continuation of Sunni orthodoxy, not an innovation; it is based on evidence and agrees with the four imams on tawhid and tanzih.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe yourself as belonging to a particular theological school, is it because you have personally examined the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, or because you trust your teachers? What would it cost you to be honest about that?
?
The author says that if affirming Allah's transcendence is called Ash'arism, then all monotheists are Ash'aris. Do you truly affirm in your heart that Allah is completely unlike His creation, or do you find yourself imagining a shape or form? What will you do today to purify your tawhid from subtle tashbih?
?
The four imams were united on the fundamentals of tawhid and tanzih—yet today Muslims often divide over these very issues. Are you contributing to unity or division? In your next conversation about Allah's attributes, will you prioritize what unites you with other believers, or will you insist on labels that separate?

Ash'ari: Reviver of Sunnah, Not Founder of a New School
Ibn Asakir refutes the claim that Ash'ari innovated a new school and explains the basis of following him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn Asakir defends Ash'ari as a reviver of Sunnah rather than an innovator, and why following him is based on evidence, not blind imitation.

Core Idea
Ash'ari revived the Sunnah and his school is based on evidence, not taqlid.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir responds to the accusation that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari invented a fifth school. He argues that Ash'ari actually revived the teachings of Ahl al-Sunnah that had become obscure and clarified ambiguous statements. He also emphasizes that adherence to Ash'ari is not blind following but based on clear evidence, and that affiliation with Ash'ari serves to distinguish true Sunnis from innovators.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the strong opening: Ash'ari is defended against the charge of innovation.
2
Identify the accusation and Ibn Asakir's response
The accusation is that Ash'ari invented a fifth school. Ibn Asakir responds that he revived what became obscure and clarified what was ambiguous.
3
Understand why following Ash'ari is not taqlid
Ibn Asakir clarifies that his own adherence is based on evidence (qiyam al-adilla), not mere imitation. This is crucial to understanding the Ash'ari methodology.
This refutes the misconception that Ash'aris follow blindly.
4
Note the purpose of affiliation
Affiliation to Ash'ari is to be distinguished from innovators like Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, etc., because Ash'ari refuted them and exposed their innovations.
The list of sects shows the context of theological debates.
